## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Bypass Audit

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in `envoyproxy/envoy` under `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/` and `source/common/tls/` that contain logic for certificate verification or validation. Specifically, identify files that reference `SSL_CTX_set_verify`, `X509_verify_cert`, `setCertificateValidationContext`, or `verify_mode`. Report which files handle server certificate validation vs client certificate validation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Audit. The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary of Findings

I identified **38 C++ source files** related to TLS certificate validation and verification across Envoy's `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/` and `source/common/tls/` directories.

### Key Distinctions:

**Server-Side Certificate Validation** (validating client certificates when Envoy acts as a server):
- **DefaultCertValidator::addClientValidationContext** - Configures client cert validation using `SSL_CTX_set_verify()` with `SSL_VERIFY_PEER` and `SSL_VERIFY_FAIL_IF_NO_PEER_CERT` flags
- **ServerContextImpl** - Initializes server contexts and calls the validation context setup
- Located in: `source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.cc:481-543`

**Client-Side Certificate Validation** (validating server certificates when Envoy acts as a client):
- **DefaultCertValidator::doVerifyCertChain** - Performs actual X509 certificate chain verification using `X509_verify_cert()` at line 315
- **ContextImpl::customVerifyCallback** - Intercepts SSL verification callbacks during handshake
- **DefaultCertValidator::initializeSslContexts** - Sets up SSL context with verification modes and trust anchors
- Located in: `source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.cc:56-192` and `280-341`

**Alternative Implementation**:
- **SPIFFEValidator** - Provides SPIFFE-specific certificate validation with similar structure but using SPIFFE trust bundles

The analysis includes specific line numbers and shows how the OpenSSL functions (`SSL_CTX_set_verify`, `X509_verify_cert`, etc.) are used for certificate validation in both directions.
